Free Talk

Memories of a Tortoiseshell Beam 139

— Yanzi

▲Wei Guangtao's Severe Interrogation of Japanese Spies

When the Sino-Japanese War broke out, Wu Dawei, the governor of Hunan, volunteered to lead troops. Observers generally considered Wu to be overestimating himself. However, there was another reason behind this. At that time, Liu Jingtang, the first-class viscount of Hunan gentry, was a famous general who revived the country during the Red Sheep Tribulation. Angered by the arrogance of the Japanese invaders, he secretly encouraged Wu to come forward and was willing to assist him. Unexpectedly, after the memorial was submitted and approved, Liu suddenly fell ill and died. Wu was at a loss and deeply regretted his rashness. After much searching, he found Wei Guangtao, a Hunan gentry, to assist him. When the army reached Jinzhou, still far from the enemy, many disguised Japanese spies infiltrated. Every day, a strict investigation was conducted, and some were always caught. Wei personally interrogated them, resorting to excessive torture. The sight was unbearable. Wei remained calm and composed, talking and laughing leisurely. Some stubbornly refused to confess, so their toes were examined. After confirming the facts, in addition to beheading, there were also methods such as "lighting the sky lantern." For a time, people called him a living Gakuro, which was by no means an exaggeration.

Talking Points from Bu Chu Ting Cao Zhai

Chinese Human Life 140

In the many useless words of the Pacific Conference, I heard a warning. Laul said, "China has nothing wasted, except human life!"

Human life! You are wasting too much in China. Old women pursue rags and rotten cotton in garbage piles, but no one cares about half-dead children starving by the roadside. Spending ten or so copper coins to hire a rickshaw puller and making him run desperately, even to the point of spitting blood and collapsing, without even looking back, one simply changes to another rickshaw and leaves. When a wife gives birth to a child, she has to hire a wet nurse. Her own child is fair and plump, while the wet nurse's child is thin and dies. A child bride who steals a piece of candy to eat is forced to hang herself by her mother-in-law. Being an apprentice is like being a slave, even having to empty the master's chamber pot. If it is not cleaned properly, a puffing pipe can crack open the head. In coal mines, one out of five people will be disabled. The Japanese come and kill hundreds at a time. A flood washes away tens of thousands. The number of people who die in a year would fill more than twenty Nanjing cities. (To be more precise, the annual death toll is more than twenty times the population of the capital.) As I write this short essay, for every word that is born, three people enter their coffins.

"China has nothing wasted, except human life!"

You must not make one-sided observations, however. When a child gets smallpox, his mother holds him in her arms for seven days and seven nights, ultimately saving his little life with outstanding perseverance and love. In this society where there is no waste but wasted lives, this great maternal love coexists. If there is a glimmer of hope, she is willing to fight for her child's life, even sacrificing her own life, and is willing to do so.

How can this great love and cold-blooded indifference coexist? What explanation is there for this contradictory society? If I raised him, I would love him as much as I love myself, or even more than I love myself. If I didn't raise him, even if tens of millions die, what does it have to do with me? This attitude explains this strange contradiction.

When will China be able to turn itself around? It will have to wait until human life is more valuable than wealth, human life is more valuable than machines, human life is more valuable than comfort, human life is more valuable than reputation, human life is more valuable than power, human life is more valuable than everything. Only when that time comes will China be able to stand up!

Writing about the Famous Ming General Qi Jiguang 141

— Qing Qu

When Japanese pirates invaded our coastal borders during the Ming Dynasty, especially in the 41st year of Jiajing, they captured Xinghua Prefecture, burning and looting everything. They then moved to Pinghai Garrison. (Established by the Ming Dynasty, the city was located east of Putian County, Xinghua Prefecture.) Since the Japanese pirates ravaged the southeast, breaking through hundreds of prefectures, counties, and garrisons, none had reached the prefectural capital. Xinghua was the first. Xinghua was a famous and prosperous prefecture. After its capture, the news shocked far and wide. An imperial decree urgently summoned Yu Dayou to be the commander-in-chief and Qi Jiguang to be his deputy to jointly suppress the pirates. At that time, Liu Xian came from Guangdong to provide aid but, with few soldiers, he fortified himself below the city walls and dared not fight. When Dayou arrived, he also did not want to attack, preferring to wait for the gathering of a large army. Thus, he and Xian separately ambushed the pirates in Changle, annihilating them. Before this, Jiguang had first defeated the Japanese pirates at Hengyu. Bringing Zhejiang soldiers to join the battle, the inspecting governor Tan Lun ordered Jiguang to command the central army, Xian the left, and Dayou the right, to jointly attack the pirates at Pinghai. Jiguang was the first to ascend the walls, followed by the left and right armies. They captured more than 2,200 heads and rescued 3,000 captured people. The Japanese pirates began to flee, and Xinghua was recaptured. Those who had invaded other prefectures and counties were also defeated by various generals. The Japanese pirates had been causing trouble for more than twenty years, attacking and breaking through cities and towns, killing and wounding officials and civilians, countless numbers. The increased transport and taxation caused unrest throughout the country. Only now, after a major defeat, did they leave. The southeast half of the country was finally able to rest in peace. Jiguang repeatedly crushed major pirates (pacifying the Japanese pirates in Zhejiang and Fujian, and also pacifying the bandits in Jiangxi), earning the title of famous general. His achievements surpassed those of Liu Xian and Yu Dayou.

Later, in the fifth month of the first year of Longqing, Wu Shilai, a supervising secretary, submitted a memorial stating that there were many alarms in Jizhou and requested that Dayou and Jiguang be summoned to specially train border soldiers. The Ministry discussed and decided to use Jiguang alone, ordering him to concurrently manage the training of soldiers in the three towns of Jizhou, Pingchang, and Baoding with the title of Vice Commander-in-Chief. Soon after, because Jizhou already had a commander-in-chief, and setting up a general manager would cause inconsistent authority, the original commander-in-chief Guo Hu was recalled, and Jiguang replaced him as the garrison commander of Jizhou, Yongping, Shanhai, and other places. Jiguang built 1,200 enemy watchtowers, each five zhang (approximately 16.4 meters) high, with a panoramic view in all directions. The hollow interior had three levels, accommodating one hundred soldiers. Armor, weapons, and provisions were all prepared. The two thousand li (approximately 1,000 kilometers) of interconnected watchtowers were strong and magnificent. He also established a chariot camp, with each chariot pushed and exchanged by four men. In battle, they formed a square formation with infantry and cavalry positioned in the middle. He also made anti-cavalry obstacles to deter enemy cavalry. When the enemy approached, firearms would be fired first. As they got closer, the infantry would hold anti-cavalry obstacles and arrange them in front, interspersed with long spears and wolf-brooms (types of weapons). When the enemy fled, the cavalry would pursue them. A supply train followed behind. He used southern soldiers as the vanguard. (At that time, the border soldiers were inflexible and undisciplined, and many were useless due to military law. Jiguang requested to recruit soldiers from Zhejiang to form an army, encouraging bravery. This was approved. Three thousand Zhejiang soldiers were stationed outside the city. It rained heavily from morning until dusk. They stood still and dared not move. The border soldiers were greatly shocked and only then did they understand military orders.) The soldiers of the Eight Guards were responsible for responding, while the soldiers of the home guard were responsible for defending. The discipline was precise, and the weapons were sharp. The military appearance of Jizhou became the best among all the borders.

Jiguang wrote nine volumes of "Practical Records of Training Soldiers": 1. Methods of Training Soldiers; 2. Training Courage; 3. Training Eyes and Ears; 4. Training Hands and Feet; 5-8. Training Camps and Formations. Within the camps and formations, he further divided them into drills, marching camps, field camps, and battle methods. 9. Concludes with Training Generals. There were more than 260 strategies for training soldiers, all aimed at training soldiers. Fearing that future generals would no longer know the methods of training soldiers, he established these articles and teachings, transmitted them in simple summaries, expressing himself carefully and with utmost dedication. He was afraid of using unsound methods and spared no effort. In addition to the "Practical Records," there were also six volumes of "Miscellaneous Collections on Training Soldiers": "General Discussion on Storing Generals" (Parts 1 and 2), "General's Arrival," "Oral Instructions on the Altar," "Explanation of Weaponry Manufacturing," and "Explanation of Chariots, Infantry, and Cavalry." There were thousands of strange and varied tactics, and even the smallest item or name was thoroughly detailed. His planning was comprehensive, and his analysis was meticulous. The reason he wrote this book with such earnestness was that if training was not done correctly, the problem was not in the lack of training, but in training without benefit. The flaw was not in not training, but in training without usefulness. Therefore, the methods of training soldiers differ from the past, but the principles of governing soldiers are the same as in the past. At this time of resisting Japan and revitalizing the army, if we also examine the war records of suppressing Japanese pirates, how could we not think of General Qi? Alas, I wish that future soldiers who lead the charge to annihilate the island barbarians would all revere him as the god of conquest.

I Kept a Cat as a Pet, but it Died from an Illness, Harmed by a Slave, and I Wrote this with Tears 142

— Chen Zhu

We depended on each other for several years.

It seemed to understand my pitiable feelings.

It accidentally suffered a minor illness and incurred someone's anger.

Then a mad slave harmed your life.

There will be no more Tiger Head flying to eat meat.

Allowing rats to run rampant.

It will be difficult to rest peacefully in the study from now on.

I lie and listen to the neighbor's rooster crowing.

My Son Graduated from the Graduate School of Cornell University in America and Sent Me a Small Photo. I Wrote a Poem to Instruct Him and to Encourage His Younger Siblings. 143

I was overjoyed to receive my son's recent photo.

I treated the distant horizon as if it were a classroom.

Son, you must strive hard to achieve fame at a young age. (A son should establish himself, practice virtue, and make a name for himself in the world. A mere graduation degree is not worth mentioning.)

When I am old and drinking wine, I will still be strong.

You must know that the responsibilities to the family and the nation are endless.

They should be as long as the rivers and the mountains.

I think my son can understand this intention.

Encourage your younger siblings to never forget.

Inscription on Mr. Huang Binhong's Painting of Guilin's Liugongtang Landscape 144

How could I get the quick scissors of Bingzhou?

To cut out half the river of the Li River's waves.

I suddenly feel like I am living in seclusion.

Looking at this, I realize that the sky is high.

I seem to hear the true master of nature speaking.

It is good to hear the old dragon roar in the deep mountains.

How much heroic sentiment did I have that day?

I drank heavily in the middle of the river, continuing the songs of Chu.

Re-Inscribing on Liugongtang Landscape Painting 145

High mountains and flowing water naturally form a village.

The place is called Liugongtang, which is most heartbreaking.

The people seem to be from the time of Xi Huang.

The mountains retain traces since the beginning of creation.

Why bother searching for the Three Mountains?

Arriving here, one forgets the reverence for the Five Peaks.

Stirring up many regrets from old travels.

Looking at the painting, I seem to still hear the monkeys.

Mr. Lin Lezhi's Admonitions 146

— Jian Fu

Lin Lezhi was an American missionary residing in China. He lived in China for forty years and maintained a literary relationship with Cai Erkang, also known as Zipu, a famous scholar in Shanghai. He was known for his proficiency in Chinese. During the Sino-Japanese War, China's survival was hanging by a thread. At that time, the Chinese people were still sound asleep. Mr. Lin felt sorry for this and thought of a way to awaken the Chinese people from their slumber. He then persuaded Mr. Cai to compile "The Sino-Japanese War Records." After this book was published, it became popular throughout the country. The Chinese people began to understand the true nature of the Japanese invasion of China. Many people know that this book was written by Mr. Cai, but they do not know that it was actually due to Mr. Lin's assistance. Otherwise, even if Mr. Cai had a sharp pen, he would have been silenced by the literary censorship of the time. However, at that time, the imperial examination system had not been abolished, and scholars competed to write patterned essays. Some admired Mr. Cai's florid style, while others admired Mr. Cai's arguments. But no one valued Mr. Lin. Mr. Lin's arguments were often full of metaphors, combining seriousness and humor. The Chinese people have always been reluctant to admit their faults and seek medical treatment. Therefore, Mr. Lin's arguments did not resonate with the common people. Mr. Lin said, "The yellow race is the giant of East Asia. In terms of intelligence, they can hold the reins of the world. It is a pity that their bodies are suffering from numbness. Acupuncture cannot awaken them, and surgery cannot make them aware. By the time their skin and flesh are empty and only their hearts remain, even if they awaken, it will be of no use." Mr. Lin's words can be said to be a painful acupuncture for the Chinese people. Now that Japanese pirates are invading, and the national territory is shrinking day by day, and the situation in the Northeast is gradually deteriorating, recalling Mr. Lin's words, I deeply hope that the Chinese people will awaken as soon as possible and treat their numbness, and not wait until their skin and flesh are empty and turn their hearts useless.

Gazing at Xiang Zhai and Chatting 147

— Gan Yi

▲Xiong Xiling

The world calls Tai Bingsan (Xiong Xiling) a phoenix, some think it's mockery because Xiling was from Fenghuang Hall in Hunan (now a county). Called such based on the place, like Zeng Guofan of Xiangxiang, or Li Hongzhang of Hefei. The Phoenix area is low-lying, small in area, sparsely populated, and full of miasma, unsuitable for long-term residence. The Qing set up a vice magistrate to govern. It is said that few survived. Therefore, in the backyard of the office, coffins were stacked, all officials who died in office. People didn't dare go. Zhu Qiyi of Changshu, a famous scholar, didn't believe the rumors. He asked the governor to give it a try. When he took office, he met Xiling. He saw Xiling as material for a prime minister. He betrothed a younger sister to him, who is now the famous Ms. Qi Hui. Chen Youming (Baozhen) of Yining, who pacified Hunan, recruited many scholars and advocated reforms. Xu Hongfu (Renzhu), the education commissioner, and Huang Gongdu (Zunxian), the provincial judge, were all fond of elegance and advocated reform. They once gathered Liang Qichao, Tang Caichang, and Xiling for a meeting to found schools, formulate regulations, and discuss new policies. During the Reform Movement of 1898, all were convicted. Xiling was already a Jinshi and a Shujishi at the time, and was also dismissed. Later, as a Daoyuan, he stayed in Jiangnan and was valued by Duanfang. He accompanied him to Japan to investigate constitutional government. Zhao Erxun specifically recommended his talent as very useful and spoke to the Minister of the Ministry of Revenue, Zai Ze. At that time, Ze was manipulating the government as a nobleman. He sought out Xiling, was amazed by his talent, and requested to fill the position of financial supervisor of Fengtian with a fourth-rank official. Ze also framed and killed his in-law, the governor of Hubei, Rui Cheng, and claimed that Xiling was good at adapting to changes. Cheng submitted a memorial recommending him as the Commissioner for Foreign Affairs of Hubei. Xiling declined the official position. He then moved to the salt transport envoy of the three eastern provinces. When the Qing Dynasty was overthrown, Xiling had already crossed the sea to the south. He spent every evening in the company of Japanese celebrities, arguing the beauty of democratic politics. After the Republic was established, he became the first Minister of Finance. He left with the Tang cabinet. Before long, he was suddenly appointed as the military governor of Rehe. He telegraphed that the army would enter. Those who were knowledgeable were shocked. Some said that he coveted the wealth of the Rehe Palace treasures and had been seeking it for a long time. After taking office, he frequently entered the palace in disguise, claiming to be an Yi Zhen and changing his title to a soldier. This was actually playing into the hands of the opposition. The post of Military Governor lacked precedent for civilians to hold. Later, someone sued him to the government. Xiang Cheng secretly ordered the Ministry of Justice to investigate and reply. Rumors are not to be trusted. Previously, when Xiling resigned and entered Beijing, he was summoned to form a cabinet. He met with Xiang Cheng. Xiang Cheng laughed and took his hand and said. "You are here, very good. The country's affairs are entrusted to someone, I have no worries. You can carefully select talents to prepare for the ministries." Xiling replied. "The scope of talent is very broad. You are not lacking in Fang Du Yao Song. I am incapable and can hardly overcome difficulties. If you must use me to mislead the country, you should choose second-rate figures to jointly praise the great cause of the founding of the country." He finished speaking and took out a list to show Xiang Cheng. The leaders of each department intended to be Wang Daxie for foreign affairs, Liu Renxi for internal affairs, Liang Qichao for finance, Shen Jiaben for justice, Chen Huan for the army, Sa Zhenbing for the navy, Fan Yuanlian for education, Zhang Qian for agriculture and commerce, and Yang Du for transportation. Xiang Cheng looked at the list and said. "These are first-class talents. I know them all. Have you obtained the consent of these people?" Xiling said. "Liu and Shen are modest. The rest are willing to help me." Xiang Cheng picked up a pen and made many changes. He handed the paper to Xiling and said. "What do you think?" Xiling agreed and withdrew. When he was appointed, Qichao became the head of justice, Daxie became the head of education, Qian became the head of agriculture and commerce, and the rest were the people who had been changed. By winter, he had been dismissed. Since then, for more than ten years, he has been drifting and supervising names, such as coal oil, river works, or disaster relief. Right and wrong, merits and demerits, are in the world. In the gengwu year, Zai Ze died. There was nothing to pay for the funeral. Moreover, he was involved in litigation due to production. Xiling quickly invited Yang Shicong, Yang Shounan, Ding Naiyang, and others to contribute some funds to stop the matter. He also set aside money for his children's clothing, food, and education expenses, which is far better than those who are friends in the morning and enemies in the evening.

Storytelling Association

Countryman Arrives in Shanghai Again (11) 148

— Bao Tianxiao

Looking out of the train window, the countryman saw rows of people with red cloths wrapped around their arms and water pipe boxes hanging from their waists. They were standing neatly, blowing tunes of "Resistance, resistance, no resistance," and beating out rhythms of "No movement, no movement, really no movement," as if welcoming someone.

"That's right, that's right!" He thought to himself again, believing his idea was not bad, and couldn't help but shout it out.

"What is it? What do you mean, 'That's right, that's right'?" The gentleman with glasses asked him.

"There must be a bride in our car. They're here to welcome the bride." The countryman was very confident that he had guessed correctly.

"Pah! Welcoming a bride would at most involve a band of Qingyin (a type of Chinese folk music) playing and singing. How could there be such a large contingent of soldiers welcoming her at the train station?" The gentleman with glasses was naturally a veteran.

"So they're all soldiers? I thought they were guests at a wedding."

"Of course they're soldiers. This playing and singing is a military band. I might as well teach you a lesson."

"How could I not know about military bands? But..."

"But what?"

"But gentry families in the city also use military bands when marrying a daughter-in-law. When my landlord, Old Master Zhang, married his third grandson's wife, didn't they also use a military band? But they wore red clothes, not yellow clothes. I still think I'm right, they're here to welcome the bride." The countryman, like a modern military expert or politician, refused to admit he was wrong and tried to defend his statement.

"What makes you think they're definitely welcoming the bride?" The gentleman with glasses was also unwilling to yield, and insisted on getting to the bottom of it.

"I can hear it from their military music. Resistance requires strength. Tonight, the bride will meet the groom, like a weak country meeting a strong country, with no resistance. Resistance requires preparation. The bride usually doesn't prepare by dancing or playing ball, so tonight she's bound to suffer. That's why their trumpets are blowing 'no resistance.' And movement also needs to be at an appropriate degree. When you can't move, you can't move recklessly. Reckless movement will cause problems. So you need to be calm. Calmness means no movement. Listen to the sound of their brass drums, they're beating out 'no movement, no movement, no movement.' That is to say, instead of moving recklessly, it's better not to move. So I say they might be here to welcome the bride."

No one listened to the countryman's nonsense, because the train had already stopped and people were pushing and shoving to get off.

Financial Last Week's Gold Market Undergoes Significant Change 149

Silver Market Frequently Rises, Exchange Rate Loosens Excessively, International News Unfavorable to the Gold Market

▲ The Disastrous Drop of 54 Taels and Change: The Gold Market Bidding Last Week Experienced an Astonishing Transformation; The Plunge Was Terrifying, The Angry Tide and Giant Waves Unstoppable, Daily Difference of Five or Six to Twenty-Odd Taels; People Were Extremely Anxious. From the Beginning of the Week, Between 680 and 690 Taels, Suddenly on Friday, It Broke Through to 630 Taels, Seeing a New Low Price of 26 Taels. The Resulting Slight Turn Was More Moderate, Returning to 640 Taels. This Week Had a Total of 67 Taels of Retrospect, Cumulatively Plummeting 54 Taels and Change, Which Can Be Said to Be Huge. This Was Due to the Overseas Silver Market's Frequent and Fierce Rises Since the Previous Thursday, Actually Exceeding 20 Pence, Marking a New Record for This Year. The Shanghai Exchange Rate Rose Accordingly, Extremely Loose and Excessive, With the Shilling Exceeding 10 Pence, and the Listed Price Lengthening by as Much as Eight Divisions. Those in the Gold Industry Generally Dumped, But the Weekend Saw a Slight Movement Towards Settlement and Offsetting Previous Shorts. Moreover, News from the International Arena Generally Affected the Gold Market, Further Exacerbated by the Increasingly Fierce Momentum of the Violent Japanese, Who Recently Brazenly Invaded the Black Provinces. Thus, Under Environmental Pressure, Although the Daily Volume of Transactions Was Not Huge, the Dalian Group Had Turned Bullish, While the Guangdong Group Still Held a Short Position. As for the Settlement Price, the Maximum Was Pressed Over 90 Taels, and the Minimum Was 50 Taels. This Was Mostly Due to the Spot Market Being Bare and Red Due to the Tight Silver Supply, and the Sluggish Sales Market Reduced Its Ability to Accept Orders. The Future Market Conditions Are Feared to Still Have Turbulence. Here Is a Summary of the General Situation During This Week:

Daily Fluctuations Are Shocking and Terrifying. Monday, November 2, Coincided with the First Day of the Preliminary Competition. Banks and Gold Exchanges, as Usual, Had Half-Day Business in the Morning. The Big Bar Lengthened Again by 3.125, to 3.125; American Silver Lengthened by 1.25; Shilling Did Not Change; However, the American Exchange Rate, Due to Exchange Differences, Contracted by 1.25, While the Internal Market Seemed to Rise. Mostly, the Gold Bidding Opened With a Small Drop of 5 Taels and 2 Mace, Calculating to 689 Taels and a Half. The Next Was 88 Taels and a Half. Subsequently, the Buyers Were Active, Rising to 93 Taels and 2 Mace. Afterwards, There Were Slight Advances and Retreats. The Morning Closed at 91 Taels and 3 Mace, Which Was Already Five Days Since the Previous Saturday, Calculating to 3 Taels and 4 Mace. In Half a Day, It Only Rose and Fell by 4 Taels and 7 Mace. The Situation Was Still Flat. The Next Day, the Big Bar Still Lengthened by 3.125, The Silver Price Lengthened by 2.5, the Shilling Lengthened by One and a Half Divisions, the American Gold Reversed and Contracted by 3.75, Again Due to the Fall in the Exchange Rate, While the Internal Market Continued to Firm and Rise. Those in the Industry All Dumped. As for the Gold Market, It Initially Was 685 Taels, With a Small Drop of 6 Taels and 2 Mace, Then Slightly Peaceful, at 88 Taels and 3 Mace. Afterwards, It Hovered Around 80 Taels. At Noon, the Atmosphere Was Bad. The Indian Exchange Rate Increased by One Lakh of Rupees. Large Accounts Dumped, Finally Dropping to 74 Taels and 3 Mace, Until the Market Closed at 76 Taels and a Half, a Wild Drop of 14 Taels and 8 Mace Compared to the Previous Day (Having Fallen 6 Days, a Total of 33 Taels and 8 Mace). There Was a 14 Taels Difference Between Morning and Afternoon. Speculator Wu Made a Balanced Move. On Wednesday, the Big Bar, the Sixth Day, Lengthened Again by 6.875. The Silver Price Halted. However, the Shilling Lengthened by Two and a Half Divisions. The Internal Market, on the Contrary, Strengthened. Truly, the Overt and Covert Trends Differed. Those in the Industry Continued to Dump Non-Stop. As for the Gold Bidding Opening, It Rebounded by 4 Taels and a Half, Calculating to 681 Taels. Mostly, the Foothold of the Big Bar Was Seen as Good. American Sellers Were Excited. The Dalian Group Was the First to Sell. Then Foreign Merchant Joseph Came to Sell, Also Because the Shilling Was Loose and Discounted. When It Fell to 77 Taels and 1 Mace, Suddenly a Rumor Spread That Someone Was Organizing a Bullish Company. People's Hearts Were Lifted, Rising to 83 Taels and a Half, But It Was All Empty Air. Soon After, Because Sellers Swarmed Up, It Broke Through Into 80 Taels. The Morning Closed at 78 Taels and a Half, Slightly Rebounding by 2 Taels. There Was a 6 Taels and 2 Mace Rotation in Half a Day. This Was a Sharp Fall With a Small Rebound. On Thursday, the Big Bar Retracted by 3.125. The Silver Price, on the Contrary, Lengthened by 2.5. The British Gold Did Not Change. The American Gold Was Listed Longer by 3.125, Due to the Exchange Rate Rebounding. The Internal Market Transaction Price Was Quite Loose. American Gold Was Especially Firm. Mostly, the Gold Market Initially Opened at 677 Taels and a Half, With a Small Drop of 1 Taels. Then, Because of More Buying, It Rose to 80 Taels and 6 Mace. Afterwards, Because of Rumors That Japan Was Again Prohibiting Gold Exports, and the Violent Japanese Invasion of the Black Provinces Was in a Tense Situation, The Market Was Filled With Clouds of Worry, Plummeting More Than Ten Taels, Breaking Through 70 Taels. At Noon, It Was Only 63 Taels and 5, Closing at 67 Taels and 7 Mace. In the Afternoon, Because the Autumn Competition Had Ended, Therefore the Afternoon Market Opened as Usual, Initially at 70 Taels. Afterwards, Suddenly Hearing That Britain Had Changed to a Silver Standard, Buying Silver Bars, The News Spread, All Firms' Selling Spirit Was Boiling, Wildly Dropping More Than Ten Taels, To 52 Taels and a Half After 4 O'Clock, Until the Market Closed at 55 Taels and 5 Mace, a Huge Drop of 23 Taels Again Compared to the Previous Day. The Fore and Aft Markets Had a Total of 28 Taels and 1 Mace of Retrospect. The Dalian Group Vigorously Sold 3,000. Joseph and Wu Both Tended to Sell Off, Aggressively Shorting. The Next Day, the Big Bar Silver Lengthened Again by 6.875. The Silver Price Lengthened by 1.5 Fen. The Shilling Lengthened by Four Divisions. Both the Overt and Covert Markets Were Loose. In a Moment, the Sellers' Power Was Flourishing, Breaking Through Into 40 Taels, To 34 Taels. However, Afterwards, There Was a Rotation of More Than 10 Taels. At Noon, It Strengthened Again, To 43 Taels and 5. At Times, It Retreated Again to 40 Taels. The Market Closed at 42 Taels and 6 Mace. In the Afternoon, 43 Taels, Then 40 Taels. The Dalian Group Competed to Buy 5,000. The Guangdong Group, On the Other Hand, Sold 2,000. On Saturday, the Big Bar Lengthened Again by 7.5. The Silver Price Lengthened by 1.25 Fen. The Shilling Lengthened by 2.5. The American Gold Lengthened by 8.75. Unexpectedly, at Noon, It Suddenly Changed to Retract by 2.5, American Gold by 6.25, While the Internal Market Tended to Strengthen. Those in the Industry Had Some Shorts to Cover. Mostly, the Gold Market Opened, on the Contrary, Rising 4 Taels and 5, To 34 Taels. Namely, the Foothold Was Good. Thursday's Market Situation Again Presented Weakness. Generally, In Light of No New Developments in the Domestic and International Situation, The Japanese Further Increased Their Reckless Cruelty, Sending Troops to the Black Provinces, Triggering the Potential of a Soviet-Russian War. Therefore, Sell-Offs Turned More Prosperous Than Buys. Bond Prices Fell One After Another, Calculating to Each Falling Back by 1.5 to 3 Yuan. Friday Still Showed Exhaustion. Changes Were Still Slight. The Market Was Slightly Better on the Weekend. The Market's Report Quoted That the United States Had Made Recommendations to Japan. Congress Was Resuming Soon. Therefore, the Buyer's Popularity Was Slightly More Prosperous. Several Types of Bond Prices Were Raised by About 1.5 Yuan. Looking at the Changes in Each Bond Throughout the Week, The Development of the External Situation Was Still the Important Reason. The Future Trend Is Still Difficult to Predict. It Will Not Deviate From This Path. However, It Is Generally Believed That the Current Bond Market Has Been Somewhat More Optimistic Than Before. Yarn and Cotton Last Week's Marked Yarn Declines 153

▲Spot Sales are Very Quiet

For a week, the yarn market has been very weak. With national affairs becoming increasingly precarious and silver becoming tighter, commerce cannot develop, the market is becoming increasingly depressed, and gold prices have plummeted and silver prices have soared. The more anxious people are, the more manufacturers have been setting up in the middle of the road, and the market has become more and more unspeakable. Therefore, the bid yarn fell below the 60-tael mark, and the prices for each month fell by 2.6-7 yuan from the previous week. The spot yarn business is extremely sluggish. Because the finances are not loose and the disaster in all directions is severe, the purchasing power should be reduced. Fortunately, there is less stock of this yarn, and the factories have emptied their existing goods and have no hoarding at all. Therefore, the spot yarn market price is still able to maintain and has not seen a big drop. The weekend is gradually trending down, it is said.

Last Week's Hankou Standard Cotton Turned Soft From Firm 154

▲ 60,000 Bales of American and Indian Cotton Were Sold

At the beginning of the week, the cotton market was very strong, and the bulls were very keen on squeezing the market due to the lack of goods coming from all directions. The stronger the pull, the more the standard cotton in each month was seen at 33 taels and 5 mace. This month, the price once reached 3 taels and 7 mace 5. However, American cotton was extremely weak. Later, due to the skyrocketing silver price, the sharp drop in gold price, and the excessive loosening of exchange rates, the silver price for imported cotton was very low. Factories absorbed large quantities, so the buyers showed an uneasy state, and the market suddenly showed loopholes. However, some bulls and cotton merchants are still holding on tightly and refusing to let go in recent months. In general, it is still dangerous. Local cotton transactions have been completely taken over by foreign cotton, and hopes for future eradication. According to the survey, the Shanghai plant of the Research Institute purchased about 600,000 bales of Indian and American cotton. Inland Hankou and other gangs imported about 200,000 bales. Tianjin is not yet included, but the number has already reached 800,000 bales. In this situation, the position of native cotton is extremely unstable. The price of standard cotton for each month fell by about 1 tael compared to the previous week. The price of American cotton was similar to last week. 60,000 pieces of American, Chinese, and Indian cotton were traded last week, it is said.

Grains and Foodstuffs, the Rice Market in Hexia Turns Stable 156

▲ Yesterday, the amount of goods arriving from each gang in Nantou was slightly less. Morning sales in urban and rural stores were calm. At first, the stomach of the trade was congested, but later, due to insufficient supply, transactions slightly recovered. Bai Geng from Sutong, Changzhou, and Xixi rose slightly. Few goods arrived of Baige and late rice, and the appetite in Ningbo was limited. Transactions on this street were extremely good, rising by a corner and a half. Very few Lyuyang Tip Grade were available, and prices fell by a corner. Old and broken Yinyuan arrived and sold evenly, and prices remained as before.

▲ Yesterday, 26 or 27 ships arrived at Xinzha. Transactions on this street were not smooth, and combined with the long sunny weather, customers were raising prices, while rice mills still had a small number of accumulations. Rural sales were very strong, and Xixin Geng was raised in stages. Baige Six Varieties were slightly raised on the stack by two chi. Not much white rice was shipped, and there was no change. Broken rice and Yinyuan had sluggish transactions and opened lower by five fen. There was no honor or disgrace for Puyang Tip, and the downstream image was presented. The trade in Kunshan rice was the healthiest, jumping sharply by three or four corners. The amount opened in Hexia was from five thousand two hundred to three hundred shi.
